## Srila Gaura Kishora Dasa Babaji | Special Discourse on Disappearance Day
**Speaker:** HDG Srila Prabhupada

### biography, renunciation, parampara
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/6zqIuMP19VM?t=56
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** biography
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Rather we should accept the instructions of our spiritual master and try to follow those instructions in our practical life."
**Summary:** This segment introduces Srila Gaur Kishodas Babaji Maharaj, his early life, renunciation, and association with Srila Bhagavad Das Babaji.

Today is the most auspicious disappearance day anniversary of one of the previous acharyas in our Sampradaya, His Divine Grace Srila Gaur Kishodas Babaji Maharaj. So a brief biography of Srila Gaur Kishodas: let us hear, and by his blessings, we will be able to advance in our Krishna consciousness by trying to follow some of the instructions that he has very nicely given us. Srila Gaur Kishodas Babaji Maharaj appeared sometime in the 1830s in the village of Vagyana in East Bengal, or Vagyana in East Bengal, which is what is now known as Bangladesh. During his boyhood, his mother and father arranged a marriage for him, and he remained in household affairs for more than 20 years. While a householder, he worked as a broker in the grain business, but even at that time, he exhibited his spirituality. After the demise of his wife, Srila Gaur Kishodas Babaji Maharaj left the country, left his business, and went to Vrindavan. There he approached Srila Bhagavad Das Babaji, one of the foremost disciples of Srila Jagannath Das Babaji Maharaj, and accepted from Bhagavad Das Babaji Maharaj the traditional Paramahamsa Vaishnava Babaji dress. After this, he became completely renounced and would stay under trees in various parts of the forest of the 168-mile Vraja Mandala or Vrindavan area. He continuously acted thus for a period of approximately 30 years. During this time, he would sometimes travel to the holy places of pilgrimage in northern and western India. Srila Gaur Kishodas Babaji Maharaj became very famous among the great devotees of Vrindavan and was awarded the appropriate title of Bhajananandi. Bhajananandi means one who is dedicated to remain in one place and chant the holy name of the Supreme Lord and completely absorb themselves in the chanting and hearing of the holy name of the Supreme Lord, but we should not try to imitate such great devotees. Rather we should accept the instructions of our spiritual master and try to follow those instructions in our practical life, while hearing the great qualities of our spiritual master and the previous Acharyas and their great deeds of devotion and service dedicated entirely for the pleasure of the Supreme Lord. Even though he received such honor, he never endeavored for even a small bit of material sense gratification and totally disapproved of the secret material desires of pseudo-renunciants and so many people who try to imitate great devotees, and prematurely they try to renounce this world, but it is not very easy to maintain the standard of renunciation exhibited by such paramahamsas as Sri Gaur Kishodas Babaji Maharaj.

---
### renunciation, bhakti, parampara
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/6zqIuMP19VM?t=301
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Srila Gaur Kishodas Babaji Maharaj accepted Srila Bhaktivinoda Thakur as his shiksha guru and Srila Bhaktisiddhanta Saraswati Thakur as his only disciple."
**Summary:** This segment describes Srila Gaur Kishodas Babaji Maharaj's devotional practices, renunciation, and his relationship with Srila Bhaktivinoda Thakur and Srila Bhaktisiddhanta Saraswati Thakur, highlighting his position in the parampara.

He would perform his pure unalloyed devotional pastimes alone in a profound devotional mood. In the year 1897, during the month of Falgunna, when he was in his sixties, Srila Gaur Kishodas Babaji Maharaj proceeded to Navadvipa Dham from Vrindavan Dham, and he did this under the instruction of Srila Jagannath Das Babaji Maharaj. From this time until his disappearance, Srila Gaur Kishodas Babaji Maharaj remained in Navadvipa Dham and in different villages. He was visiting the various places of pastimes of Lord Gauranga, and he was realizing the non-difference between Navadvipa Dham and Vrindavan Dham. He begged by gathering dry foodstuff from the householders of the holy Dham. He would sometimes offer these foodstuffs to the Supreme Personality of Godhead by simply holding them in his hand. He was totally renounced, so he didn't have any elaborate arrangements for offering or cooking or anything like that. In order to cook, he would collect dry wood from the footpath, and he would wash earthen pots discarded by the villagers along the roadside near the Ganges River on the occasion of eclipses. These are considered totally impure, but a renunciant has nothing to do with purity and impurity of this world. Just he would take something of no value to others, and somehow, with those bare minimum things, he would maintain himself. This would actually ensure that such great devotees are never entangled in any material endeavors. They save time, maximum amount of time, for their spiritual activities exclusively. In order to clothe himself, he would go to the shore of the Ganges and collect and wash discarded cloth that had been used to cover dead bodies at the burning heart. This was his level of renunciation. Thus he always remained independent of the support of others simply by utilizing items of no value to others. In such a manner, he obtained the practical necessities of life. In 1897, Srila Bhaktivinoda Thakur constructed his place of bhajana on the bank of the Saraswati River at Godurma Dvipa, one of the nine islands in Navadvipa, called Svananda Sukhada Kunja. This is the name Srila Bhaktivinoda Thakur gave to that building he constructed. This was a gathering place for exalted souls, for great devotees. Here, Srila Bhaktivinoda Thakur recited and explained the Srimad Bhagavatam and other topics regarding the conclusion of devotional service, and Srila Gaur Kishodas Babaji Maharaj would come and hear these talks with great delight. In this way, Srila Gaur Kishodas Babaji Maharaj accepted Srila Bhaktivinoda Thakur as his shiksha guru. Also, Srila Gaur Kishodas Babaji Maharaj accepted Srila Bhaktisiddhanta Saraswati Thakur as his only disciple. That's how you see in our parampara, His Divine Grace A.C. Bhaktivinoda Swami Prabhupada, the founder Acharya of ISKCON. His guru is Srila Bhaktisiddhanta Saraswati Thakur. His guru is Srila Gaur Kishodas Babaji Maharaj, and his shiksha guru is Srila Bhaktivinoda Thakur. This is the parampara in which Srila Prabhupada, the founder Acharya of ISKCON, is coming. So Srila Gaur Kishodas Babaji Maharaj is the spiritual master of the spiritual master of Srila Prabhupada.

---
### renunciation, devotion, purity
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/6zqIuMP19VM?t=574
**Verse References:** BG 9.26
**Content Type:** story
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "The important aspect of the offering, more than the item itself, is the devotion with which that offering is made."
**Summary:** This segment describes Srila Gaur Kishodas Babaji Maharaj's possessions, his understanding of scriptures, and two incidents illustrating his teachings on purity and devotion, emphasizing the importance of offering with devotion rather than material contamination.

His only possessions, if at all you may consider them as possessions, were the Tulsi beads he wore around his neck, this Kanti Mala, and the Tulsi Mala he kept in his hand for counting his rounds. His Kanti Mala and his Japa Mala were his only two possessions. He also kept a few books, such as Narottam Das Thakur's Prarthana and Prema Bhakti Chandrika. These are two famous books, books written by Narottam Das Thakur, containing a collection of the songs he has composed, explaining the pure devotional service. Even though it appeared that Gaur Kishodas Babaji Maharaj was not a learned Sanskrit scholar, still the purport and conclusions of all scriptures were luminous in his heart and character. It is described in the scriptures that chanting of the holy name reveals all transcendental knowledge within the heart, and this is practically seen in the life of Srila Gaur Kishodas Babaji Maharaj. He knew all the conclusions of the scriptures without studying them separately. That is because his chanting was pure. We should not imitate this. It was never possible for anyone to serve him, for he was never willing to accept any kind of service from any person. He exhibited the highest standard of devotion to the Supreme Lord Sri Krishna, and because of his exemplary character, he was recognized as the personification of the deepest degree of separation from Lord Sri Krishna, Vipralamba Seva, service in separation from Krishna. This is what is taught by Sri Chaitanya Mahaprabhu, especially in our Gaudiya Vaishnava Sampradaya, because in separation from Krishna, one feels intense mood of service to Krishna, not as much as when one is in the presence of Krishna. It is more intense than in the presence of Krishna. In separation from Krishna, one is able to serve with more intensity Krishna with that intense feeling of devotion towards Krishna. There are many incidents recorded by biographers about his preaching. Even though he is called a bhajananandi, he would not travel and actively preach, but anybody approached him for getting guidance, for getting some practical instructions, he was ever willing to give them his divine association. So I will just mention one or two such incidents which are very instructive for all of us. Once a lawyer by name Bhattacharya brought several sweets and prayerfully requested Srila Gautishwada's Babaji Maharaj to accept his offering. Srila Babaji Maharaj told him, "I never take any sweets." So then Bhattacharya replied, "There is nothing higher than accepting food that the Lord has directly accepted, indicating thereby that it is Prasadam. Why are you refusing Prasadam?" So then Srila Babaji Maharaj, Gautishwada's Babaji Maharaj, sharply retorted, "Whoever eats fish is like a prostitute." These are harsh words, but then they are required to cut through the several layers of illusion that is clouding the consciousness of our condition. So if someone has perverted desires and offers foodstuffs to Lord Chaitanya, these preparations can never be accepted as the Prasad of the Supreme Lord because the Lord does not partake of them. What does Krishna say in the Bhagavad Gita? Yome Bhaktya Prayacchati Patram Pushpam Phalam Toyam Yome Bhaktya Prayacchati. The important aspect of the offering, more than the item itself, is the devotion with which that offering is made. So Krishna, what does he want when we offer? He wants devotion. He wants Bhakti. So somebody is having lusty desires in his heart and then makes a show of offering, that is not accepted by Krishna. To offer foodstuffs to the Supreme Lord that have been contaminated by one's lusty desire should be considered a great offense. That means it is against our devotional interest. If one accepts the grains of a sinful person, then his mind becomes impure. This is very important for all of us, that why do we say eat only Prasadam, don't eat food that is not offered to Krishna, because we do not know sometimes the source of such food could be, if it is not properly offered to Krishna, then it could be from the sinful person, and then that contaminates our mind, so we should be very careful not to accept anything which is not Prasadam properly offered to Krishna. Thus one is directed by Babaji Maharaj not to accept food cooked by lustful persons, especially by those who know the actual standard of behavior expected of devotees of Sri Krishna, but who nevertheless indulge knowingly in illicit activities. So this is very, very important for us to remember, knowingly one should never indulge in sinful activities at the same time perform devotional service, especially offering of food stuff to the Supreme Lord.

---
### association, devotion, illusion
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/6zqIuMP19VM?t=976
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** story
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Please take note that these sadhus who speak sharp words to drive away the witch of the illusory energy are actually the only real devotees of Krishna and friends of the living entities."
**Summary:** This segment recounts two incidents where Srila Gaur Kishodas Babaji Maharaj gives instructions, one about the contamination of the mind by eating food offered by materialistic people, and another about the importance of associating with devotees even if they speak harshly, as their words can drive away illusion.

Sri Chaitanya Mahaprabhu instructed Srila Swaroop Damodar Goswami as follows: when one eats food offered by a materialistic man, one's mind becomes contaminated, and when the mind becomes contaminated, one is unable to think of Krishna properly. A contaminated mind is not conducive for any form of devotional service. Our practice becomes obstructed. Srila Gaukishodas Babaji Maharaj always gave beneficial instructions to persons who approached him with faith and humility, no matter what their spiritual status might have been. On one such occasion, a seeker went to Babaji Maharaj to hear topics concerning the Supreme Lord, but he heard some harsh words from him instead. The seeker therefore resolved never again to go near Babaji Maharaj because he was feeling hurt by the harsh words spoken by Gaukishodas Babaji Maharaj. After some time, however, when he was very much distressed in his mind, he decided to go and see Babaji Maharaj. So Srila Gaukishodas Babaji Maharaj could immediately understand the reason for the depression of this particular seeker, and he told him, "You have left the association of devotees where topics about Krishna are discussed, and now you are living in a secluded place performing solitary worship of Krishna. When one hears the topic of Supreme Lord in the company of devotees, then one becomes freed from Maya's net of illusion, but if someone performs worship of the Lord in a secluded place, not in the association of devotees, one becomes caught by the material illusory energy of the Lord. As a consequence, instead of topics about the Supreme Lord possessing the heart, mundane subject matters will occupy the heart." The seeker replied, "I thought it better to reside in a secluded place and perform my own individual worship than to become disturbed by hearing the sharp words of a sadhu." He thought if I remain with a sadhu and the sadhu speaks very harsh words, then my mind will always be disturbed. I can peacefully go to some other place and do my own worship and be nicely situated to do devotional service. So Babaji Maharaj replied, "Please take note that these sadhus who speak sharp words to drive away the witch of the illusory energy are actually the only real devotees of Krishna and friends of the living entities. When a devotee of the Lord, who is always desirous of the living entity's ultimate welfare, chastises him just once with instructions meant to drive away maya, then that living being immediately makes plans to leave the saintly persons for his entire life. If you actually want to perform devotional service properly, then you must accept the harsh language of the sadhu as the medicine by which maya can be given up. It's just like when a doctor prescribes a medicine, even if it is bitter, you take it because you know that only by taking the proper medicine, even if it is bitter, it will cure you of your ailment or disease, so you should not look for something that is tasting sweet when it comes to taking medicine. Similarly, the harsh words of a sadhu may sound like very, very hurting, but actually they are meant simply to pull you out of illusion, which is the purpose of your doing devotional service. By this one can obtain the necessary spiritual advancement to successfully chant the holy name of the supreme lord."

---
### detachment, family life, devotion
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/6zqIuMP19VM?t=1258
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "As long as one remains in bodily consciousness, one cannot obtain the mercy of Krishna."
**Summary:** This segment presents another instruction from Srila Gaur Kishodas Babaji Maharaj regarding Vaishnavas living with their wives, emphasizing the importance of inner detachment and spiritual energy gained through chanting, contrasting genuine Vaishnava behavior with superficial renunciation.

Then another instance, one other person, he inquired from Srila Gaurakeshwara's Babaji Maharaj as follows: he said, "We see that there are many Vaishnavas living with their wives who perform devotional service to Lord Hari. Will they get any benefit from such service?" Srila Babaji Maharaj replied, "The living entity is the eternal servant of Lord Krishna, but when the conditioned soul looks upon his wife and son simply by seeing their material external forms, then one does not have the eye of devotion, and he can never perceive his real identity as the eternal servant of Krishna. The conditioned souls always have inclination to enjoy their wives and children, that's natural, and they don't like to hear so much the topics of the supreme lord or to get association of the lord's devotees. If one does not attain the spiritual energy given by chanting the holy name, then one will become attracted by his wife and children. Then again, there are other persons who externally want to detach themselves from their wives and children and sense enjoyment, but they don't have any kind of external renunciation without actually having that detachment within the heart is like the renunciation of monkeys, markata vairagya, this is what it's called, and although they externally live away from their possessions, but their heart is dirty, the heart is not clean. So what is the characteristic of a monkey? A monkey lives naked, so it doesn't even have a piece of cloth, it doesn't have a proper house, it lives simply on the ground, it lives on the ground. So the monkey has the desire to enjoy so many female monkeys, not just one. Every male monkey will have so many male monkeys as a devotee or an ancient should reflect the inner detachment or should at least aim it also simultaneously strenuously trying for detachment from within the heart. The genuine vaishnava will never maintain an attitude of sense gratification towards his wife and children, but he will always regard himself. Those actually desirous of performing Haribhajana but in whose heart the weeds of material desires grow and were unable to give up excessive attachment of their wife and children should always try to hear from pure devotees and chant Hare Krishna and perform congregational chanting. Instead of leaving their family and going away to a secluded place, one should actually engage in such activities even while remaining in family life. In this way they can quickly become detached from the inclination to enjoy materially. Then they will gradually realize that if one completely surrenders to Krishna, then one will attain all the qualities of life. This is called auspiciousness. As long as one remains in bodily consciousness, one cannot obtain the mercy of Krishna.

---
### disappearance, controversy, purity
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/6zqIuMP19VM?t=1550
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** story
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "I am the sole disciple of Paramahamsa Srila Gaurakeshwara das Babaji Maharaj."
**Summary:** This segment describes Srila Gaur Kishodas Babaji Maharaj's passing away and the controversy surrounding his samadhi, highlighting Srila Bhaktisiddhanta Saraswati Thakur's bold assertion of his discipleship and challenge to those with impure lives, ultimately securing the right to prepare the samadhi.

So in this way, Gaur Kishore das Babaji Maharaj taught what is real renunciation because he himself was a real renunciate. Then regarding his passing away, on November 16, 1915, Gaur Kishore das Babaji Maharaj entered the eternal pastimes of the Lord, Nitya Leela Pravishta. That means he passed away from this world. That day at sunrise, his disciple Srila Bhaktisiddhanta Saraswati Thakur left Sri Mayapur for the place where Srila Bhaktisiddhanta, sorry, Gaur Kishore das Babaji Maharaj had been staying in a place at Kuliyam. The head priest of Navadvipa's various temples and ashrams began to argue where would Babaji Maharaj's samadhi be made, the actual place. So there was a heated argument among so many different people. So because there was a material motive, whoever got the opportunity to prepare the samadhi of this great Paramahamsa, Srila Gaur Kishore das Babaji Maharaj, they would have huge number of people visit their temple and get handsomely from the pilgrims. So with this material motive, there was so much of argument. So Srila Bhaktisiddhanta Saraswati Thakur could understand their material motive and he wanted to actually stop them from simply creating a controversy. Now, not only Srila Bhaktisiddhanta Saraswati Thakur wanted to avoid the controversy, but even the Navadvipa's inspector of police, whose name was Jathindra Sinha at that time, he arrived at that place apprehending some breach of peace. So after much discussions, the other Vaishnavas who were running different ashrams and mats, they stated their position to the inspector. That Saraswati Thakur is not a sannyasi. He has no right to prepare a samadhi for a person who is completely renounced. Hearing their pronouncement, Saraswati Thakur replied in a voice like thunder, "I am the sole disciple of Paramahamsa Srila Gaurakeshwara das Babaji Maharaj. Even though I have not accepted sannyas, I am a celibate brahmachari and by the grace of Babaji Maharaj, I am not hypocritical, renunciant, addicted to abominable habits." So he put a challenge for those people who within the last one year or six months or three months or just even one month or even three days has not indulged in illicit association with women will be able to touch the spiritually blissful body of Srila Gaurakeshwara das Babaji Maharaj. If anyone else touches the body, he will be completely ruined. Hearing these words, the inspector of police asked Srila Saraswati Thakur, "How will evidence for this be produced?" So Saraswati Thakur replied, "I will believe whatever they say. Let them just tell it. That's all." After this challenge is offered, all the other Babaji's, they turned their backs and went away one by one. That means they all accepted that they were not leading a pure life. The inspector was dumbfounded. Then, Srila Bhaktisiddhan Saraswati Thakur actually prepared a nice samadhi and laid to rest the blissful transcendental body of Srila Gaurakeshwara das Babaji Maharaj. So let us end this presentation with the prayer to Srila Gaurakeshwara das Babaji Maharaj. Namo Gaurakeshwaraya Sakshad Vairagya Murtaye Vipralambhara Sambhode Padambhu Jayate Namaha. The meaning is, I offer my respectful obeisances unto Srila Gaurakeshwara das Babaji Maharaj, the spiritual master of Srila Bhaktisiddhan Saraswati Thakur, whose renunciation personified Sakshad Vairagya Murti, he is always merged in a feeling of separation from an intense love of Krishna. Hare Krishna.

## Srila Prabhupada Clarifies the Caste System | @madhupanditdasaofficial | ISKCON Bangalore
**Speaker:** HDG Srila Prabhupada

### caste system, misinterpretation, cultural criticism
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/S1oFJfM8UU8?t=0
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Congregation / volunteers, Newcomers
**Key Quote:** "Especially, it has been rooted in western universities to deprecate India's culture and say that there is a caste system which is the biggest evil in the society."
**Summary:** The speaker discusses how excerpts of Prabhupada's teachings are being used to criticize the Vaishnava tradition and perpetuate the idea that the caste system is evil.

Just take somebody who was saying, there was one video where Prabhupada says, "Shudra is fourth class. They carry out the orders of the others." Somebody put it on YouTube. The person cuts and pastes only that and puts it. And people are criticizing Prabhupada. "Oh, see, they have a caste system." Simply bringing sentimentalism over, Shudra means you are lower than Brahmana. Especially, it has been rooted in western universities to deprecate India's culture and say that there is a caste system which is the biggest evil in the society.

### nature vs nurture, Krishna consciousness, surrender
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/S1oFJfM8UU8?t=147
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Come surrender to Krishna and develop Vaishnava culture, Brahmanical culture."
**Summary:** The speaker uses the analogy of a lawyer's son to illustrate the influence of environment, but emphasizes that training is essential, and that Krishna consciousness allows one to transcend even their own nature, inviting all to surrender to Krishna and develop Vaishnava culture.

If you are the son of a high court judge, because of legal vibrations in the house, you have got good chances of you also becoming a lawyer. That does not mean that just because he is born, he will become a lawyer. He has to train him. And that is what Krishna consciousness movement is doing. And when you become a Vaishnava, even karma you cross, you will be able to do work which is not even your nature. If that work is for Krishna, you will transcend even karma. We do not care. Your birth is Brahmana, Kshatriya, Vaishya, Shudra, we do not care. Come surrender to Krishna and develop Vaishnava culture, Brahmanical culture.

## Srila Rupa and Sanatana Goswami: Lives of Surrender and Service | Sri Gaura Mandala Parikrama
**Speaker:** HDG Srila Prabhupada

### lineage, incarnation, devotion
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/sDOmqVy2GoY?t=0
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** story
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Being pure devotees, Rupa and Sanatana always lived in the mood of separation from the Lord and his abode."
**Summary:** This segment details the genealogical history of Rupa and Sanatana Goswami, their birth, family, education, and their initial service under Nawab Hussain Shah, highlighting their devotion and eventual separation from worldly life.

Jiva Goswami has explained the genealogical history of Sri Rupa Goswami's family. They were the descendants of Sarvagya Satguru, a great scholar of the Vedas. He was an expert in Yajur Veda. Sri Sarvagya was a Brahmin and also one of the kings of Karnataka in the 12th century Shakabdha. In his lineage appeared a great devotee named Kumara Deva who had settled in Jaishur, Bangladesh. He got married to a very chaste lady named Revati Devi. In the course of time, Kumara Deva and Revati Devi gave birth to many sons. Most illustrious among them were Amara, later known as Sanatana Goswami, Santosha, known as Rupa Goswami and Vallabha, known as Anupama. It is believed that Sanatana was born around 1488 AD, while his younger brother Rupa appeared in this world around 1493 AD. It is mentioned in the Adi Leela of Sri Chaitanya Siddhartha Amritha that Sri Rupa, Sanatana and Anupama are the 43rd, 44th and 45th branches of Mahaprabhu's Desire Tree of devotion service and that they are the best of all. Anupama Vallabha Sri Rupa Sanatana etina shakha vrkshera paschime sarvottama. Sri Kavikarnapura reveals in Gauraganodesha Deepika that Sri Rupa Goswami was none other than the incarnation of Sri Rupa Manjari, one of the chief assistants of Lalitha Sakhi, one of the eight principal gopis of Vrindavan. Sri Sanatana Goswami was the combined incarnation of Rati Manjari and Lavanga Manjari and Sanatana Kumara. Jiva Goswami, the son of Anupama, was the incarnation of Ilaasa Manjari. After Kumara Deva had died, these three brothers came over and settled here at Malda, where they continued with their studies. As they grew up, they became exceptionally attractive to all of the society. They possessed beautiful bodily features, noble character and natural compassion towards every living being. They were embodiments of the Lord's love. These three brothers studied the science of logic, Nyaya, and the knowledge of the divine. They were also the descendants of Madhusudana Vachaspati, who was the brother of Sarvabhauma Bhattacharya. They also became proficient in Sanskrit, Arabic and Persian. When Sanatana Goswami was very young, he saw a dream in which a Brahmin gave him a copy of Srimad Bhagavatam. The next day, to his surprise, he indeed received Srimad Bhagavatam. From then on, Shri Sanatana began scrutinizingly studying Srimad Bhagavatam, leaving aside all other scriptures. Bengal, during that time, was under the Mughal rule of Nawab Hussain Shah. He is the same king who had employed Shri Mukunda Dasa of Shrikhanda as his personal doctor. Seeing the popularity of Shri Rupa and Sanatana amongst the great general populace, the Nawab decided to employ them as his ministers. In this way, he planned to bring the entire Hindu population under his control. If Rupa and Sanatana joined him, then his subjects would become more submissive, he thought. On the other hand, he notified Shri Rupa and Sanatana, telling them that if they became the ministers, he would award the Vaishnavas and Hindus with all freedom. Instead, if they did not accept his proposal, then he would torture and prosecute the masses. Hearing the king's warning, Shri Rupa, Sanatana and Anupama reluctantly agreed to serve the king. Their service was so exemplary that Shri Sanatana Goswami was made the Prime Minister of Bengal and Rupa Goswami was made the Home Minister. Due to their close proximity with the Muslims, the two brothers were excommunicated from the Hindu society by the orthodox caste Brahmins of Gaur Mandala. Thus, Shri Rupa Goswami came to be known as Dabarkhas and Shri Sanatana as Sakaramalik. The king grew very fond of them and considered them his own brothers. He awarded them with tremendous amounts of wealth and power. They settled down here at Ramkeli in Malda, where they constructed beautiful opulent palaces and gardens that served as a replica of Vruddhavan. Being pure devotees, Rupa and Sanatana always lived in the mood of separation from the Lord and his abode. Here at Ramkeli, the beautiful temples and ponds dug by our Goswamis are still present.

---
### divine encounter, devotion, mercy
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/sDOmqVy2GoY?t=350
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** story
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Rupa Goswami glorified Sri Chaitanya and revealed that he was none other than the Supreme Personality of God and Himself."
**Summary:** This segment describes Lord Chaitanya's visit to Ramkeli, the impact he had on the people, and the Nawab's reaction. It highlights Rupa Goswami's bold declaration of Chaitanya as the Supreme Personality of Godhead.

The beautiful deity of Shri Madana Mohana that was installed by them over here continues to accept our humble services till this day. They held the highest post in the government as they were very rich, yet the Goswamis did not possess even a grain of pride. People, scholars, Vaishnavas from all parts of the country would come to meet them and they would worship them with most intimate hospitality. Their humility and simplicity captured people's heart. There was a beautiful piece of architecture that we came across while visiting. This marvelous victory tower known as Firoz Minar is more than 26 meters in height. According to reliable sources, this tower was engineered by Sanatan Goswami while he served as Bengal Gov. Lord Chaitanya, during his second attempt to reach Vruddhavan, decided to take a roundabout route. Actually, his desire was not travelling to Vruddhavan, but instead he wanted to meet and shower his mercy upon Sri Rupa and Sanatana. Thousands of men accompanied the Lord during his journey. All of them were surcharged with deep ecstatic feelings, completely devoid of external consciousness and surrendering themselves completely. They sang and danced along. An ocean of love flooded the people with waves after waves of ecstasy. As the procession reached new places, more people joined. Wherever the Lord touched the ground with his lotus feet, people immediately gathered to take the dust. The people took out so much dirt that holes were created in the ground. Just by seeing the smiling face of the Lord, all their lamentations and unhappinesses became vanquished. Eventually, the Lord arrived at Ramkeli, where innumerable people arrived to take his darshan. Performing Sankirtana over here, the Lord danced and sometimes lost his consciousness out of intense love of God. When Nawab Hussain Shah came to know that Lord Chaitanya was attracting so much attention, he was astonished. His spies informed him how Mahaprabhu had immersed everyone in a wave of transcendental ecstasy. He learned how the people, irrespective of their caste, creed or religion, were raising their hands and engaging in the congregational chanting of Hare Krishna, Hare Krishna, Krishna Krishna, Hare Hare, Hare Rama, Hare Rama, Rama Rama, Hare Hare. So the Nawab then asked Keshava Chhatri whether he knew anything about Lord Chaitanya. Keshava, in spite of knowing everything, tried to diplomatically downplay the situation. He replied that Chaitanya Deva was simply a touring mendicant and that only a few people had come to see him. He warned the King against considering the advice of his spies too seriously. After pacifying the King in this way, Keshava sent a Brahmana messenger to Lord Chaitanya, requesting him to leave without delay. The King then inquired from Rupa Goswami Dabarkas and asked his opinion. Rupa Goswami glorified Sri Chaitanya and revealed that he was none other than the Supreme Personality of God and Himself. He added that it was the Nawab's great fortune that the Lord has chosen to descend and manifest his pastime in this country. It was only by Mahaprabhu's mercy that the Nawab was enlightened. The Nawab was successful and victorious in all his affairs.

---
### humility, surrender, divine guidance
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/sDOmqVy2GoY?t=594
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** story
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Out of great humility, the two brothers held straw between their teeth and fell down like a rod before Mahaprabhu."
**Summary:** This segment narrates the incognito meeting of Rupa and Sanatana with Lord Chaitanya, their display of extreme humility, and the Lord's acceptance and blessings. It also covers their advice to the Lord regarding the Nawab's unpredictable nature and the large following.

Sri Rupa and Sanatana then began considering how they could meet Lord Chaitanya incognito. Thus, in the dead of the night, the two brothers went to meet the Lord. First, they met Nityananda Prabhu and Haridas Dhaka who introduced them to Sri Gaurahari. Out of great humility, the two brothers held straw between their teeth and fell down like a rod before Mahaprabhu. They were so overwhelmed that they began crying in joy. They introduced themselves as the lowest of men who were employed in the worst kind of employment. They glorified the Lord as Patitapavana, the deliverer of the fallen, and assured him that none in the world qualified as being more fallen than them. Out of sheer humility, they declared themselves millions of times more fallen than even Jagai and Madai, the sinful brothers whom Lord Chaitanya had previously delivered. Jagai and Madai are millions of times more virtuous. Adhamma and Patita are sinners. We are two people. Thus, they tried to establish themselves as the befitting candidates upon which Lord Chaitanya should shower his costless mercy. Hearing their prayers, Lord Chaitanya became very pleased and blessed them wholeheartedly. He then revealed that the two brothers were his eternal servants. Mahaprabhu also informed them that he had received several of their letters, which reflected their humble state of mind and consciousness. He accepted them and awarded them the name Rupa unto Dhabi's caste and Sanatana unto Sakara-Malik. The Lord also revealed that he had come to Ramkali only to meet and bless the two of them. He assured them of his protection and asked them not to worry. He added that they would be delivered very soon. The two brothers then sought the blessings of the Vaishnava's presence. Before leaving, however, they humbly cautioned the Lord that although the nabob was favorable at that moment, his mood was unpredictable. By nature, the nabob was a very dangerous and a very violent man. Hence, they suggested that it would be better if Mahaprabhu departed from that place without further delay. They also added that it would not be very appropriate for Mahaprabhu to travel to Vrindavan, accompanying such thousands of followers. Instead, it would be more befitting if Mahaprabhu went alone, accompanied by a select few. Having spoken thus, the two brothers offered prayers unto the lotus feet of the Lord and returned to their homes. Although Sri Chaitanya was the Supreme Lord himself, yet he acted like a mere human. In order to teach us neophytes how to react in such situations, heeding the advice of Rupa and Sanatana, he decided to leave that village.

---
### renunciation, detachment, service
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/sDOmqVy2GoY?t=791
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** story
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Srila Prabhupada highly glorifies and hails this as a perfect example of how one should divide his money and retire from one's household life."
**Summary:** This segment describes Lord Chaitanya's departure and Rupa Goswami's actions to renounce his wealth, distribute it to various parties, and facilitate Sanatana's escape from service.

In the morning, he left for a place called Kanenaarsala, where he relished many past times of Lord Krishna. Then, thinking about the words of Sanatana, Mahaprabhu concluded that it would indeed not be proper to travel to Vrindavan with so many followers as it might disturb the atmosphere of the dhamma. Thus, he decided to return to Jagannath Puri. On returning to Puri, the Lord disclosed to his intimate associates how he had bestowed his most intimate mercy upon Rupa and Sanatana, owing to their humility and pure devotional qualities. Rupa Goswami took all his treasures and loaded them into a boat. He and his younger brother, Anupama, left for their ancestral home at Fateh Bar, presently in Bangladesh, where they distributed all their wealth. He appointed a brahmana to perform auspicious ceremonies so that they might obtain the shelter of Mahaprabhu. Of his wealth, he gave 50% charity to the brahmanas and Vaishnavas and 25% to his relatives. Srila Prabhupada highly glorifies and hails this as a perfect example of how one should divide his money and retire from one's household life. He also deposited 10,000 gold coins with a grocer in order to help Sanatana Goswami to escape. Sri Rupa Goswami kept one-fourth of his wealth aside with a respectable brahmana for his personal safety and emergencies. Srila Rupa Goswami then set out with two men to find out where Mahaprabhu was, when Mahaprabhu would be leaving for Vrindavan from Jagannath Puri. The men came back with news that Lord Chaitanya had already left. Sri Rupa immediately wrote a letter to Sanatana Goswami informing him of the news. He also added that he and Anupama were living immediately from Vrindavan and asked Sanatana Goswami to set off as well. He also informed his elder brother that he had left 10,000 gold coins with a grocer to help him escape.

---
### liberation, instruction, empowerment
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/sDOmqVy2GoY?t=931
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** story
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "By entering into Rupa's heart, Mahaprabhu empowered him to ascertain the conclusions of all truth."
**Summary:** This segment details Sanatana Goswami's refusal to serve the Nawab, his imprisonment and escape, and Rupa Goswami's meeting with Lord Chaitanya at Prayag, where he received extensive instructions on Krishna Tattva, Bhakti Tattva, and Rasa Tattva.

Meanwhile, Sanatana Goswami stopped going to the office and would just remain at home reading and chanting Srimad Bhagavatam all day. In the assembly of devotees, Nawab Hussain Shah came to his residence to enquire about Sanatana's health as he thought he was sick. Seeing that he was perfectly fit, the Nawab asked Sanatana to assist him in attacking the province of Orissa. Sanatana Goswami refused to obey the order of the king and expressed his desire to retire from service instead. The king became enraged and ordered Sanatana's arrest. Using the money that Rupa Goswami had kept for him, Sanatana Goswami managed to bribe the jailer and somehow escaped. The jailer was initially reluctant to release him, but 7,000 gold coins were enough to change his position. On being released, Sanatana immediately crossed over the Ganges and fled. He passed through hilly terrains and spent the night at a small hotel on his way to Benares. The hotel owner, knowing that Sanatana's servant Isha had eight gold coins in his possession, wanted to murder both of them and take away the money. However, Isha could guess the evil plans of the hotel owner and voluntarily offered him the coins and sought his help to safely reach his destination. Thus, the owner helped them cross the hilly track and proceed towards Varanasi. The two brothers, Rupa and Anupama, meanwhile, met with Sri Chaitanya Mahaprabhu at Prayag, Allahabad. The two of them had straws between their teeth and surrendered themselves at the lotus feet of the Lord. Lord Chaitanya embraced the two brothers and placed his feet upon the head. It was here at Prayag, at the Dvadasva Medha Ghat, that Lord Chaitanya had instructed Sri Rupa Goswami for ten days, empowering him in the philosophy of devotional service. He taught Rupa the limit of Krishna Tattva, Bhakti Tattva, the truth regarding the transcendental mellows, culminating in conjugal love between Radha and Krishna, Krishna Tattva, Bhakti Tattva, Rasa Tattva, Pranata.

---
### literature, devotional service, essence
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/sDOmqVy2GoY?t=1089
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Bhakti Rasamata Sindhu contains the essence of all the revealed scriptures."
**Summary:** This segment describes Lord Chaitanya's instructions to Rupa Goswami to excavate holy places, discover deities, write literature, and preach. It also lists the significant books written by both Sanatana and Rupa Goswami, highlighting the importance of Bhakti Rasamata Sindhu.

He also taught him the ultimate conclusions of Srimad Bhagavatam. By entering into Rupa's heart, Mahaprabhu empowered him to ascertain the conclusions of all truth. Teaching him thus, Lord Chaitanya sent Rupa Goswami to Vrindavan, instructing him to excavate the holy places of Krishna's pastimes, discover the ancient deities that lay hidden in the Vrindavan and reinstall them in his temples, write transcendental pieces of literature and preach the Vrindavan way of worship to the entire world. The summary of Lord Chaitanya's teaching to Rupa Goswami has been summarized by Srila Rupa in the teachings of Lord Chaitanya. So those who want to read more about the teachings can read the teachings of Lord Chaitanya or Chaitanya Chaita Amrita. It is said that Lord Chaitanya had taught the four principal qualities of a Vaishnava through four of his intimate associates. He had taught the quality of self-control through the life and examples of Ramananda Raya, the quality of neutrality through Damodara Pandita who even scolded Mahaprabhu at times, the aspect of tolerance through Haridas Thakur and the quality of humility through Sanatana Goswami. Among the books that Shri Sanatana Goswami had written, Hari Bhakti Vilas and Brihat Vaishnava Toshani are significant. Amongst the books composed by Shri Rupa Goswami, Hamsa Dutta, Uddhava Sandesha, Krishna Janma Tithi Vidhi, Radha Krishna Ganodesha Deepika, Sthava Mala, Vidakta Madhava, Lalita Madhava, Dhanakeli Kaumotuki, Bhakti Rasamata Sindhu, Ujjvala Neelamani, Akshyata Chandrika, Mathura Mahima, Padhyavali, Nataka Chandrika, and Laghu Bhagavata Amrita are the most significant. Bhakti Rasamata Sindhu contains the essence of all the revealed scriptures. Shri Srinivas Acharya in his prayers unto the six Goswamis hence glorifies them as expert in extracting the essence of all the revealed scriptures with the aim of establishing the Jeeva in his eternal position of performing pure devotional service unto Krishna.

---
### pastimes, worship, legacy
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/sDOmqVy2GoY?t=1248
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** story
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Both Rupa and Sanatana travelled extensively through Vraja Mandala, discovering many pastimes, places of Radha Madhava."
**Summary:** This segment describes the Goswamis' travels, their simple living, their dedication to writing and chanting, and their establishment of deity worship. It also mentions the current state of the temples and deities in Ramkeli.

Both Rupa and Sanatana travelled extensively through Vraja Mandala, discovering many pastimes, places of Radha Madhava. Having no fixed residence, they would catch a few wings of sleep, no more than one and a half hours per day, under a tree or bush. They used to live by whatever little they obtained, by performing Madhukari, Shri begging from door to door. Shri Rupa and Sanatana spent all their time writing, discussing Krishna pastimes, and chanting Krishna's holy names. Shri Rupa Goswami established the worship of Shri Radha Govinda Dev in Vrindavan, while Shri Sanatana inaugurated the worship of Shri Madan Mohana. Both of these enchanting deities are currently being worshipped in Rajasthan. So the different things we see in Ramkeli here are the temples. That is this temple where we are sitting. That is Radha Madan Mohan Deity, established by Rupa and Sanatana. We also have Balarama and Revati. And they also established Chaitanya. Three Deities of the Pancha Tattva. Pancha Tattva have five personalities. But installed three personalities here. Chaitanya Mahaprabhu in the middle. Nityananda on the left. And Advaita on the right. So three personalities they installed here. There is this Keli Kadamba tree, under which Chaitanya Mahaprabhu met Rupa and Sanatana. And there is a small temple. And the entrance of Govinda Hari's lotus feet. There is Rupa Sagar, a large pond excavated, by Sri Rupa Goswami. We will see here. There are also eight sacred ponds, little far away around this place. Just outside the temple gate, is a beautiful deity of Lord Chaitanya, that had been installed over here, by Jeeva Goswami. The dancing hall surrounding this temple, has been renovated and restored to its health, with help of, here also, Bhaktivedanta Goswami's charitable trust, has given money to renovate this temple, Srila Prabhupada's trust. There is also the prison house, where Sanatana Goswami was present, imprisoned by the Nava. Then there is also, a little away, a Rose Minar, which was constructed by Sanatana Goswami. Sri Sanatana Goswami Ki, Naya, Sri Lama Padukhe, Taigood, and Premanande.

### devotion, knowledge, mystery
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/SqSgsKehYQI?t=0
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "That very ancient science of the relationship with the Supreme is today told by me to you because you are my devotee as well as my friend."
**Summary:** This verse is important to understand the Bhagavad-gita because it is a mystery that can only be understood by a devotee in intimate relation with Krishna.

Translation: That very ancient science of the relationship with the Supreme is today told by me to you because you are my devotee as well as my friend. Therefore you can understand the transcendental mystery of this science.

So why he selected Arjuna? He was a military man. He was not a Vedāntist. A military man is not supposed to become a Vedāntist, very great sannyāsī. No. Because the so-called Vedāntists, they cannot understand Bhagavad-gītā. It is not possible.

### relationship with God, creation, fatherhood of God
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/SqSgsKehYQI?t=350
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Newcomers, General public
**Key Quote:** "Sambandha means what is my relationship with God."
**Summary:** The first departmental study in the Vedas is sambandha, which means understanding our relationship with God, who is the source of everything, and Krishna explains that He is the original father of all living entities.

First thing is sambandha. Sambandha means what is my relationship with God. This is stated there. In the Vedānta it is said, janmādy asya yataḥ. The absolute truth is that from whom everything is generated. So everything amongst everything I am also. You are also. So you are also coming from that supreme absolute truth. Kṛṣṇa says, mam evāṁśa jīva-bhūtaḥ. All these living entities, sarva-yoniṣu kaunteya, in every species, any form of life, saṁyavanti-mūrtaḥ, as many forms are there, not only human being, the animals. The trees, the birds, the aquatics, the insects, everyone, all living entities. Kṛṣṇa says, sarva-yoniṣu kaunteya saṁyavanti-mūrtaḥ. In any species of life, as many forms are there, ahaṁ vija-pradabhitāḥ. I am their original father. Vija-pradabhitāḥ, seed-giving father. So as father places the seeds within the womb of the mother, similarly the material nature is the mother, and Kṛṣṇa is the father. Kṛṣṇa impregnates the material nature, and we come out in different forms.

Bed bugs, because if you keep your bed nasty, do not keep it very clean, then by your perspiration there is generation of these bed bugs. They are called seda-ya, by perspiration. And anda-ya, through the eggs, just like the birds, the living entities coming through the eggs. That is called anda-ya. Seda-ya, anda-ya, jarā-yuja, embryo. Just like we are coming from the embryo, anda-ya, jarā-yuja, and udvija. Coming from the seeds, the trees, plants. So within these four groups, all different living entities are coming. If you become saintly person, but if you remain rogues, thieves, cats and dogs, then how you can see God? You have to become a santah. If you remain always addicted to sinful activities, how you can see God? That is not possible. You have to give up this, just called sinful activities. What are the sinful activities? Illicit sex, meat-eating, intoxication and gambling. That's all. You have to give up this. If you become leader, so-called leader, rascally leader, and you are addicted to illicit sex and intoxication and meat-eating, you must be seated. If you are sinful, how you can lead person?

### Kṛṣṇa-kathā, peacefulness, relief
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/CPaYBnLBlsg?t=30
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers, Newcomers
**Key Quote:** "The world is like the blazing fire in the forest, so this Kṛṣṇa-kathā, this Kṛṣṇa consciousness movement, will give them relief."
**Summary:** Engaging in Kṛṣṇa-kathā, talking and questioning about Kṛṣṇa, brings peacefulness and relief from the blazing fire of the world.

So, questioning about Kṛṣṇa and answering the question is Kṛṣṇa-kathā. So here it is recommended that if we are constantly engaged in Kṛṣṇa-kathā, about Kṛṣṇa, talking about Kṛṣṇa, questioning about Kṛṣṇa, then ātmāṣu prakṛtati. We are hankering after peacefulness of our heart, peacefulness of our atmosphere. So here it is recommended that simply by inquiring about Kṛṣṇa and taking answer of the question, both the questioner and the answer-giver, both will be pleased. Jaya ātmāṣu prakṛtati. Therefore Caitanya Mahāprabhu ordered, yāre dākṣa tāre kaha kṛṣṇa-apare. The world is like the blazing fire in the forest, so this Kṛṣṇa-kathā, this Kṛṣṇa consciousness movement, will give them relief. Jaya ātmāṣu prakṛtati.

### spiritualism, materialism, Kṛṣṇa consciousness

**Summary:** The distinction between materialism and spiritualism lies in whether we remember Kṛṣṇa; forgetting Him is materialism, while remembering Him is spiritual.

Now the question is, how the foods and stores which is matter, become spiritual? Isn't that the question? We say one man is constructing this type of a building with wood and stone. We say this is materialistic. They can also challenge you that you are also interested in wood and stone and constructing a huge church or temple. Why? Why in your... Yes, spiritualism. Now, you can compare. This is spiritualism means in this stone and earth and wood you remember Kṛṣṇa. I am constructing something for Kṛṣṇa. Therefore it is spiritual. So the conclusion is when we forget Kṛṣṇa, that is materialistic. And when we constantly remember Kṛṣṇa, that is materialistic.

### bhakti, karma, sense gratification
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/CPaYBnLBlsg?t=912
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers, Newcomers
**Key Quote:** "Materialism means forgetfulness of Kṛṣṇa. Otherwise there is no materialism."
**Summary:** Actions performed for the satisfaction of Kṛṣṇa are bhakti and spiritual, while actions performed for sense gratification are karma and materialistic, ultimately materialism is forgetfulness of Kṛṣṇa.

But the same thing done for the satisfaction of Kṛṣṇa, that we shall construct this temple for Kṛṣṇa's inauguration. We shall construct this building for providing devotees of Kṛṣṇa so that they may be able to chant Hare Kṛṣṇa mahā-mantra without any disturbance. It appears the same thing, karma and bhakti. But bhakti is always in relation with Kṛṣṇa, and karma is always in relation with sense gratification. Therefore the thing, the ingredient, is originally spiritual, because it is Kṛṣṇa's energy. But ahaṁ mamṛti, when we try to impose our proprietorship, that is materialism. Materialism means forgetfulness of Kṛṣṇa. Otherwise there is no materialism.

### purpose of knowledge, infallible purpose, Krishna consciousness
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/x4pl2rq9V70?t=39
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "If you can explain the activities of Kṛṣṇa, how He is acting, how the chemical process is going on under His direction, if you can write a thesis on this subject matter, then ultimately Kṛṣṇa is behind that, then your study of chemistry is perfect."
**Summary:** The speaker explains that the true purpose of knowledge, including scientific knowledge, is to understand and glorify Krishna, recognizing Him as the ultimate cause and director of everything.

Now, śāstra says that avicchito artha, artha means purpose. If somebody asks what is the purpose of becoming a scientist, what is the purpose of becoming a physicist? So different men will give different answers. It is meant for this purpose, it is meant for this purpose. But kavi bhi, those who are actually learned, advanced learning, they have said that avicchito, avicchito means without any failure, without any contradiction. You say that chemistry is required for this purpose. I say chemistry is required for this purpose. Another man says chemistry is required for this purpose. But difference of opinion, that is not accepted. Avicchito, infallible purpose. What is that infallible purpose? Avicchito artha. Kavi bhi nirupita. Nirupita means it is already settled. You haven't got to make research anymore. Nirupita means it is already settled. It is already concluded. What is that? Yad uttama-sloka-guṇa-anuvarnanam. If you can explain the activities of Kṛṣṇa, uttama-sloka, how He is acting, how the chemical process is going on under His direction, if you can write a thesis on this subject matter, then ultimately Kṛṣṇa is behind that, then your study of chemistry is perfect. Aviccita-artha-kavirbhi-nirupitam.

Nirupitam, it is concluded. No more argument. That is the purpose. That means if you are intelligent enough, actually, then through any source of knowledge you come ultimately to Kṛṣṇa. That mayādhyakṣeṇa prakṛtiḥ śrūyate śrī-cāryaḥ. Actually everything is being done by His potency. Here there are different tests. The material is the same, but the method of mixing the material, different tests are coming out in existence. So how that expertly management of mixing is going on, if we can explain by our chemistry, by our mathematical values, then our studying of the material is going to be very, very good. So the understanding of chemistry is perfect. Then we are perfect.

### devotion, glorification of Krishna, humility
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/x4pl2rq9V70?t=387
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "A devotee neither claims anything, neither claims anything. He is not taking any credit for himself. Neither it is possible. Even he may be very, very big devotee, he will never claim any credit for his glorious activities. His glorious activities means to make Kṛṣṇa glorious."
**Summary:** The speaker explains that a true devotee uses their knowledge to glorify Krishna, taking no credit for themselves, and that Krishna is pleased when He sees that the knowledge He has given is being used for His glorification.

That is haritauśana. Unless Kṛṣṇa sees that you are trying to glorify Him by your knowledge, then He becomes satisfied that I have given Him some knowledge, and He is utilizing this knowledge for my glorification. He is my devotee. Devotee's business is to glorify. He doesn't take any credit for himself. Actually there is nothing to be taken, credit. All credit goes to Kṛṣṇa. A devotee neither claims anything, neither claims anything. He is not taking any credit for himself. Neither it is possible. Even he may be very, very big devotee, he will never claim any credit for his glorious activities. His glorious activities means to make Kṛṣṇa glorious. Not that like the so-called materialist, he takes, wants to take the credit. No. Sakarmanā tam abharcho saṁsiddhī davate naraḥ. Sakarmanā. You may be engaged in any pattern of work, any department of work, but by dint of your work, you establish the existence of God, Kṛṣṇa, and whatever is being done, it is being done by the expert management of Kṛṣṇa.

Don't think the sun is working so nicely. Automatical, not automatical. The master is there, Kṛṣṇa. The sun is so powerful substance within this universe. There are many millions of suns. This is one sun only. But it is carrying out the order of Kṛṣṇa.

### Krishna's potencies, unlimited energy, spiritual reality
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/x4pl2rq9V70?t=541
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Similarly, the Supreme Lord, by expanding His potencies by His energy, He remains the same. He does not diminish."
**Summary:** The speaker describes the unlimited nature of Krishna's energy, using the sun as an analogy to explain that even after giving unlimited heat and light for millions of years, it remains the same, and similarly, Krishna's potencies are inexhaustible.

yaccha kṣuresa śavitā śagala-grhānā rājā samastha śra-mṛti aśeṣu tezā Aśeṣu tezā. Unlimited. Light. Unlimited fire. Unlimited heat. Aśeṣu. Aśeṣu tezā. There is no compression. With the sunlight, sunset, there is no compression within this universe. Unlimited. For millions and millions of years, it is from the sun, the light and heat is coming out, but there is no diminution. They, it is the same as it was millions of years ago, and after giving you light and heat for millions of years, the same quantity of light and heat is still there. So if it is possible for a material thing, that after giving unlimited heat and light, it remains the same. Similarly, the Supreme Lord, by expanding His potencies by His energy, He remains the same. He does not diminish. Purnasya purna-mādāya purna-mī-bhāva-śuṣyate. So if we can see in the material object that the heat being emanated from many millions and millions, it remains the same heat. It maintains the same heat, same life. Why it is not possible for the Supreme? Therefore, Īśvara-bhūta-paṇiṣāda informs us that purnasya purna-mādāya purna-mī-bhāva-śuṣyate.

The disciples inquired from the guru, why you are crying, sir? No, I have finished everything. I have given you everything. I have given you everything. Therefore, I am now finished. That is not spiritual. That is material. I have got hundred rupees. If I pay you hundred rupees, then my pocket is empty. But Kṛṣṇa is not like that. Kṛṣṇa can make hundreds of thousands and millions of Kṛṣṇa, still He is Kṛṣṇa. That is Kṛṣṇa. The potency is never exhausted. That is called purnasya purna-mādāya purna-mī-bhāva-śuṣyate.

### Humility, Material Fall, Surrender
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/jsbOXtHRf6Y?t=68
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Although they are fallen, if they simply submit themselves at the lotus feet of Shri Chaitanya Mahaprabhu, they will be saved from sinful reactions."
**Summary:** This segment covers Sanatana Goswami's humble submission and self-identification as fallen, followed by an explanation of how he, despite being from a brahmana family, considered himself fallen due to association with meat-eaters and materialists, and how surrender to Shri Chaitanya Mahaprabhu can save one from sinful reactions.

Text 98. Putting a straw in his mouth and bowing down, Sanatana Goswami clasped the lotus feet of Shri Chaitanya Mahaprabhu and humbly spoke as follows. Text 98. Putting a straw in his mouth and bowing down, Sanatana Goswami clasped the lotus feet of Shri Chaitanya Mahaprabhu and humbly spoke as follows. Translation. Sanatana Goswami said, I was born in a low family and my associates are all low class men. I myself am fallen and am the lowest of men. Indeed, I have passed my whole life fallen in the well of sinful materialism. Actually, Shri Sanatana Goswami belonged to a brahmana family because he belonged to the Saraswati division of the brahmanas and was well-cultured and well-educated. Somehow or other, he accepted a ministership in the Muslim government. Therefore, he had to associate with meat-eaters, drunkards and cross-materialists. Sanatana Goswami considered himself fallen for in the association of such men, he also fell victim to material enjoyment. Having passed his life in that way, he considered that he had wasted his valuable time. This statement about how one can become fallen in this material world is made by the greatest authority in the Gaudiya Vaishnavasam Pradaya. Actually, the whole world is presently fallen into material existence. Everyone is a meat-eater, drunkard, woman-hunter, gambler and what not. People are enjoying material life by committing the four basic sins. Although they are fallen, if they simply submit themselves at the lotus feet of Shri Chaitanya Mahaprabhu, they will be saved from sinful reactions. This ends the Bhaktivedanta Parbat.

### Humility, Social Status, Service
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/jsbOXtHRf6Y?t=917
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Because service is meant for the śūdras, not for the brāhmaṇas, kṣatriya and vaiśya."
**Summary:** This segment elaborates on Sanatana Goswami's self-identification as belonging to a lower caste, explaining that although he was born into a brahmana family, his acceptance of a ministership in the Mohammedan kingdom, which was considered service, placed him outside the brahmana community, as service was traditionally meant for the sudras.

Now, why He is submitting himself? Nīca-jāti. Nīca-jāti means those who are born in lower family. They are called nīca-jāti. They are śūdras or less than the śūdras. According to Vedic system, the brāhmaṇa, kṣatriya and vaiśya, they are higher caste. And the śūdras, they are lower caste. And less than śūdras, they are lowest. So Sanātana Gosvāmī, actually he belongs to the brāhmaṇa family. He, his forefathers belonged to the śārasya-brāhmaṇa family. There are different set, gaura-brāhmaṇa and śārasya-brāhmaṇa. So śārasya-brāhmaṇa, actually, they belong to the Aryan, āryavartā, the Panyāra side and Kashmir side. They are considered high-class brāhmaṇas. So he belongs to that community. But somehow or other, their forefathers… I mean, make their domicile in Bengal. Because they had some property in Bengal. They are very rich, aristocratic family. And this Sanātana Gosvāmī accepted ministership in the Mohammedan kingdom. So in those days, amongst the brāhmaṇa community, if any brāhmaṇa would accept service, he becomes at once a śūdra. He becomes at once. Because service is meant for the śūdras, not for the brāhmaṇas, kṣatriya and vaiśya. They would never accept anybody's obligation as service. They would starve. That was the principle. Only the śūdras could accept service. So because these Sanātana Gosvāmī and Rupa Gosvāmī accepted government office, although it was government office, but it was service, so they were outside the brāhmaṇa community.

No. You should first of all try to understand whether he is actually fit. Then offer yourself. So just like Sanātana Gosvāmī, when he first saw Caitanya Mahāprabhu, he did not offer himself. ### Haridasa Thakur, Puliya, Chanting, Miracle
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/ZboVSgUlJxk?t=232
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** story
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Understanding their fear, Haridasa Thakur spoke to the snake and told them, My dear snake, because of the fear of you, devotees are hesitant to come here and chant with me."
**Summary:** This segment describes Haridasa Thakur's life in Puliya, his dedication to chanting 300,000 names of Krishna daily, and the miracle of him asking a poisonous snake to leave the cave, which increased the villagers' devotion to him.

Lord Brahma appeared as Haridasa Thakur, stayed here in this Puliya village at this place. There used to be a cave in this place during those days and a tree where Haridasa Thakur would spend most of his time chanting the names of Lord Shri Krishna. He would chant 300,000 names of Lord Shri Krishna every day. He would cry. He would dance. Sometimes he would fall unconscious chanting the names of Lord Shri Krishna. Villagers would come here to take association of Haridasa Thakur and chant with him. But the villagers also noticed there was a black poisonous snake living in the same cave which posed a great threat to Haridasa and other visitors. So they were very hesitant to visit the place. Understanding their fear, Haridasa Thakur spoke to the snake and told them, My dear snake, because of the fear of you, devotees are hesitant to come here and chant with me. If you don't mind, could you please go somewhere else and live or if you are uncomfortable leaving this place, I would like to go and be somewhere else. With the words of Haridas Thakur, the black snake immediately left the place and went away. Seeing this miracle, the villagers were struck with awe and reverence. Their respect and devotion to Haridas Thakur increased immensely. This wonderful pastime happened at this place where Haridas Thakur stayed and performed his Nama bhajana.

### immortality, intelligence of God, Hiranyakasipu
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/OevVtXN2A5k?t=0
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers, Newcomers
**Key Quote:** "God is always more intelligent than ourselves. We should always remember."
**Summary:** Srila Prabhupada explains that everyone in the material world must die, and Hiranyakasipu tried to avoid death in a materialistic way, but Krsna is more intelligent and cannot be cheated.

Wherever you go within this material world, either in the Brahma-loka or in the Patala-loka, you have to die. That is the problem. So Hiranyakasipu wanted to solve this in a materialistic way, but that is not possible. So in a negative way, he wanted that I shall not die on the land, I shall not die in the air, I shall not die in the water, I shall not be killed by any man-made weapon. In so many ways, negatively, he thought that he has become immortal. But Krsna is so intelligent that keeping all the words or the blessings given by Lord Brahma to Hiranyakasipu, He cannot kill anyone. So we cannot cheat God. That is not possible. However scientifically we may be advanced, God is always more intelligent than ourselves. We should always remember.

### universal kinship, Krishna as Father, compassion
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/ewOaJaDBsak?t=376
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Congregation / volunteers, Newcomers
**Key Quote:** "Therefore, a devotee of Krsna does not want to commit a little harm to any living entity."
**Summary:** Srila Prabhupada elaborates on the concept of universal kinship, stating that Krishna is the Supreme Father of all living beings, and therefore a devotee of Krishna does not want to harm any living entity.

Actually, everyone is our sa janam because if God is father, as Krsna claims, ahaṁ vīja-pradapitāḥ, if He is the Supreme Father, not only He claims, at least any fine religious system claims God is the original Father. That's the fact. ahaṁ sarvasya prabhava matta-sarvaṁ prabhartate. Everything has come from Him. He is the Supreme Father. If Krsna is the Supreme Father, He is father of everyone. sarva-joni-sukha-antaya sarva-joni-sukha-antaya. In all species of life, in all forms of life, they are all our sa janam, kinsmen. How it cannot be? Because Krsna is the original Father. This is Krsna consciousness. Therefore, a devotee of Krsna does not want to commit a little harm to any living entity. That is Krsna consciousness. sarva-joni-sukha-antaya sarva-joni-sukha-antaya sarva-joni-sukha-antaya sarva-joni-sukha-antaya sarva-joni-sukha-antaya sarva-joni-sukha-antaya sarva-joni-sukha-antaya sarva-joni-sukha-antaya sarva-joni-sukha-antaya sarva-joni-sukha-antaya sarva-joni-sukha-antaya sarva-joni-sukha-antaya Yukta-cuse.

### spiritual vision, soul's dimension, karma
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/ewOaJaDBsak?t=574
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "The living part, the soul is the same dimension either within the ant or in the elephant."
**Summary:** Srila Prabhupada explains that a Krishna conscious person sees everyone as part of the same family, regardless of their external form, because the soul within each being is of the same dimension.

The same member of the same family. It does not matter if one has become ant or one has become elephant. The living part, the soul is the same dimension either within the ant or in the elephant. This dimension of the soul we have several times discussed. One ten thousand part of the top of the air. kesagra satavagasya satadhā kalpitasya ca jīva-bhāga-sabhījña sa anantāya kalpate. There is the dimension. In śāstra we get the dimension of the soul. Very, very minute. One ten thousand part of the top of the air, just a minute. So that portion is within the ant and within brahmā and within elephant. Therefore, one who is pundit, one who knows what are these soul spiritual parts, part and parcel of Krsna, if he has got full knowledge, then his vision is vidyā-vinaya-samparni brāhmaṇi govī-hasthini śunite ca sapāke ca paṇḍitāḥ samadarsana. Samadarsana means equal vision. A learned brāhmaṇa is most intelligent man in the human society. And a dog superficially, externally, there is much difference. Here is a dog, a street dog, and here is a learned brāhmaṇa. But one who is pundit, one who is Krsna conscious, he sees that the pundit and the dog, they are the same, because they are also the same spiritual part. By his karma, he has become a learned pundit. And by his karma, he has become a dog.

That is called brahma-jñāna. So when one attains this brahma-jñāna, then brahma-bhūta-prasannātmā na śocati na kānta samas sarveṣu bhūteṣu samatā equal. That is brahma-jñāna. So in this verse, Arjuna says that yad rājya sukha-lobhena hantuṁ śva-janam pūrdhataḥ. So when we are killing animals for the satisfaction of our tongue, this is mahāpātaḥ. If we want to kill anyone, any living entity, for my satisfaction, either my tongue satisfaction or any sense satisfaction, it is mahāpāpaṁ, great sinful act.

### universal family, sense gratification, real happiness

Because they are all śva-jana. You cannot kill. Either you take this sense or that sense. But Arjuna is speaking in a limited sense. He is thinking of his own family members. And if I kill him for my satisfaction, my sense satisfaction, it is great sinful act. Unfortunately, everyone is killing for his sense satisfaction, gratification, in the name of religion. In the name of religion, in the name of religion, and although it is prohibited, still they are killing. Thus, imagine how much sinful activity they are doing and how they can be happy. But that is not happiness. Happiness is different thing. sukhaṁ ātyam tṛtaṁ yatraṁ atindriya grāhyam. If you want to feel happiness by your, this blunt material senses, that is not happiness. Happiness is beyond your material senses. ātyam tṛtaṁ. That is real happiness. Real happiness means it will never end. And you will never feel satiation. There is no more want. That is real happiness.

### material vs. spiritual happiness, purified senses, Krishna's satisfaction
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/ewOaJaDBsak?t=917
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Whatever we do for our own sense satisfaction, that is mahāpā, sinful activities. But if we do the same thing for Krsna's satisfaction, that is spiritual advancement."
**Summary:** Srila Prabhupada contrasts material and spiritual happiness, explaining that real happiness is beyond the material senses and is achieved when our senses are purified and used for the sake of Krishna.

Material happiness, there is no such thing. That you will feel immediately satiation. After enjoying any material happiness, a few minutes, you will feel again another, again another, again another. So, therefore, in the Bhagavad-gītā it is said, sukhaṁ ātyam tṛtaṁ yatraṁ. So, real joy, what is real happiness, that is not felt by these blunt material senses. What is that sense? That is purified senses. sarva-pādhi-vinirmuktaṁ tat-paratyena nirvana. When our senses are purified, tat-paratyena, for the sake of Krsna, when our senses are employed for the sake of Krsna, that is purified senses. rīśi-keṇa rīśi-keśa-sevanam bhakti-rīcchate. That is wanted. So, here, in the beginning, Arjuna is thinking in terms of his blunt senses. But the same thing he will do. He will do. ātyam tṛtaṁ atindriyaḥ purified senses. Just try to understand. This is Krsna consciousness. Arjuna is now thinking yad rājya-sukha-lobhena. For the matter of getting kingdom and sense gratification, I am going to kill my kinsmen. So it is great sin. That's a fact. If the warfare, in the Kuruksetra battlefield, was for Arjuna's sense satisfaction, then it was a great sin. But actually it is not being done for Arjuna's satisfaction. It is to be done for Krsna's satisfaction. So therefore the conclusion should be that whatever we do, if we do it for our own sense satisfaction, that is mahāpā, sinful activities. But if we do the same thing for Krsna's satisfaction, that is spiritual advancement. This is the difference. So outsider, they think that a karmī is working for his own satisfaction, and a devotee is working for Krsna's satisfaction. Although two things are, similarly, externally it appears the same thing, but there is great difference.

Whatever you do for your own satisfaction, for the satisfaction of your whims, that is mahāpā, great sin. The same thing, when you do for Krsna, that is opening your path to liberation, back to home, back to God. This is difference. You have to change the consciousness, what you are doing, for whom you are doing, for yourself or for Krsna. This is Krsna consciousness. And that is the perfection of life. In whatever position you are, whatever you are doing, it doesn't matter. That is confirmed in the Śrīmad-Bhāgavatam. adapyaṁ vīdīyaśreṣṭa-varṇāśrama-vibhāgaśaḥ sānuṣṭhitaśya-dharmanāṁ saṁsiddhī-haritauśanaṁ haritauśanaṁ means to satisfy the Supreme Lord. That is perfection. It doesn't matter what you are doing. varṇāśrama-vibhāgaśaṁ. First of all, whatever doing, it does not mean whatever nonsense you are doing. That will be accepted. No. varṇāśrama-vibhāgaśaṁ. God is the one who makes you happy. He is the one who makes you happy. He is the one who makes you happy. He is the one who makes you happy. He is the one who makes you happy.

### Varnashrama, Vedic civilization, satisfying Krishna
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/ewOaJaDBsak?t=1179
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "But if you act for the satisfaction of Krsna according to the prescription of your position, then your life is perfect. That is wanted."
**Summary:** Srila Prabhupada defines Varnashrama according to Vedic civilization, emphasizing that activities must be done according to prescribed duties, and perfection is achieved when those duties are performed for the satisfaction of Krishna.

So that's the definition of varṇāśrama. According to Vedic civilization, there is division of varṇa. Brāhmaṇa, kṣatriya, vaiśya, śūrya. So activities must be done according to the varṇāśrama prescription. A brāhmaṇa is ordered to do like this. Satyamādhama titikṣhā, aryava. So that is, therefore, it is called varnāsana. The prescribed duties are already there. Therefore perfect human society means, first of all, there must be this division. Brāhmaṇa, kṣatriya, vaiśya. And when they act the duties of that particular position, brāhmaṇa, kṣatriya, for the satisfaction of Krsna, that is perfection of life. It doesn't matter whether you are a śūdra or you are brāhmaṇa, but if you act for the satisfaction of Krsna according to the prescription of your position, then your life is perfect. That is wanted.
