Those who are for increasing money, mercantile mentality, they should be also collected. Similarly, śūdras. And they should be trained, everyone, to satisfy Krsna. Varnāsamo vibhāgasaḥ sānuṣṭitasya dharmasya saṁsiddhiḥ hṛtośaḥ. So here Arjuna is a fighter. He is engaged in fighting. Now he is thinking that is proper. He is Vaisnava. He is devotee. No. That is not Krsna's business. Although superficially it appears that Krsna is engaging Arjuna to fight in the sinful activities. No. That is not sinful. Whatever Krsna does, it is not sinful. It is transcendental. The most pure activity. Therefore one, the rascals who do not understand Krsna, they say that Krsna is immoral.

### sun analogy, purification, Krishna's influence
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/ewOaJaDBsak?t=1456
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** analogy
**Audience:** Newcomers, General public
**Key Quote:** "Similarly, even though somebody comes to Krsna with some purpose which is not moral, but the man or woman who comes there, he becomes, he or she becomes purified."
**Summary:** Srila Prabhupada uses the analogy of the sun evaporating water from both clean and filthy places to illustrate that Krishna's influence purifies even those who approach Him with impure motives, without Krishna becoming tainted.

He, just like the sun, is very powerful. As we see in this material world, the sun, a material thing, and it is very powerful. But the sun is soaking water, taking water from the sea as well as from filthy place. See, He is also taking, what is called soaking? Evaporating, yes. Evaporating water from urine also. And fill the place where ditches. He is evaporating water as well as from the sea. But it does not mean by evaporating water from the sweat, ditch and urine, the sun is becoming polluted. No. Rather He is turning that place, what is called, prophylactic, antiseptic, by His sun sign. Similarly, even though somebody comes to Krsna with some purpose which is not moral, but the man or woman who comes there, he becomes, he or she becomes purified.

## Who is Humble and Meek? | HDG Srila Prabhupada | Bg 1.43 | 22.07.2024

### Bhagavad Gita, Family Tradition, Hell
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/xQNqH9zvCXQ?t=0
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "O Krishna, maintainer of the people, I have heard by disciplined succession that those who destroy family traditions dwell always in hell."
**Summary:** Srila Prabhupada reads verse 43 from Chapter 1 of the Bhagavad Gita, along with its translation and purport, emphasizing the consequences of destroying family traditions.

Om Namo Bhagavate Vasudevaya. Reading from Srimad Bhagavad Gita, Chapter 1, Observing the Armies on the Battlefield of Kuruksetra, Verse number 43: Utsanna kula-dharmāṇāṁ manuṣyāṇāṁ janārdana narake niyatam vāso bhavatīty anuśuśruma. Translation and purport by His Divine Grace A.C. Bhaktivedanta Swami Srila Prabhupada: O Krishna, maintainer of the people, I have heard by disciplined succession that those who destroy family traditions dwell always in hell. Purport by His Divine Grace A.C. Bhaktivedanta Swami Srila Prabhupada: Arjuna bases his argument not on his own personal experience but on what he has heard from the authorities; that is the way of receiving real knowledge. One cannot reach the real point of factual knowledge without being helped by the right person, one who is already established in that knowledge. There is a system in the varnasrama institution by which one has to undergo the process of ablation before death for his sinful activities. One who is always engaged in sinful activities must utilize the process of ablation, called the Prayaschitta. Without doing so, one surely will be transferred to the right path. One who is engaged in sinful activities will not be transferred to the left path. One who has been engaged in sinful activities should be transferred to hellish planets in order to undergo a miserable life as a result of sinful activities. This is Bhaktivedanta's purport. Bhaktivedanta Swami Srila Prabhupada. O Krishna, maintainer of the people, I have heard by disciplined succession that those who destroy family traditions dwell always in hell. Bhaktivedanta Swami Srila Prabhupada.

This is meant for the human being, Manuśyāna, not for the animals. So unless the human society accepts these principles of varnasana-dharma, ordained by Kṛṣṇa, the Supreme Lord, it is not considered amongst the human beings. ### Goal of Life, Sadhya-Sadhana, Darwin's Theory
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/xQNqH9zvCXQ?t=234
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Congregation / volunteers, Newcomers
**Key Quote:** "Sādhya means what for this human form of life we have got. That is called sādhya, the goal, the goal of life."
**Summary:** Srila Prabhupada introduces the concepts of sādhya (the goal of life) and sādhana (the means to achieve that goal), contrasting it with Darwin's theory, which he criticizes for lacking a clear understanding of life's purpose.

Therefore in the Viṣṇu Purāṇa, when Caitanya Mahāprabhu was talking with Rāmānanda Rāya, so Caitanya Mahāprabhu inquired, what is the actual aim of life? Sādhya-sādhana. Sādhya and sādhana. What is the aim? Sādhya means what for this human form of life we have got. That is called sādhya, the goal, the goal of life. And sādhana. Sādhana means the activity by which we can attain, we can achieve that goal of life. This is called sādhya-sādhana. The Darwin theory, although they are given some idea of progressive evolution, but he does not know what is the goal of life, why this progress is there. That these rascals, they do not know. They simply just imagine it.

## Why Seek the Shelter of the Supreme Lord? | Srila Prabhupada

### devotion, material desires, benefits of Krishna worship
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/616K-1_1lPo?t=0
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers, Newcomers
**Key Quote:** "Kṛṣṇa will fulfill your material desires and at the end will give shelter at His lotus feet."
**Summary:** This segment explains that while people seek temples for material gains, worshiping Kṛṣṇa fulfills desires and ultimately grants shelter at His lotus feet, unlike worshiping demigods which offers temporary and finite benefits.

People generally go to temples and churches for mitigating some material wants. Even if you have material desires, still you take shelter of Kṛṣṇa. Kṛṣṇa will fulfill your material desires and at the end will give shelter at His lotus feet. This is the advantage of devotion and service. Whereas if you worship other demigods, you may get some temporary benefit, but at the end the benefit will be finished, you will be finished, and the demigod who has given you the benediction, he will also be finished. But even one has got some material desires to be fulfilled, if he worships Kṛṣṇa, that desires will be fulfilled. At the same time, he will get shelter under the lotus feet of the Lord. This is the advantage.

**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Krishna is the Supreme Personality of Godhead, no one is equal to or above him, he is the primeval Lord or Bhagavan known as Govinda and he is the supreme cause of all causes."
**Summary:** This segment explains the three phases of understanding the Absolute Truth: Brahman, Paramatma, and Bhagavan, using the analogy of the sun and establishing Krishna as the Supreme Personality of Godhead.

Of life they do not lead to higher planets but to infamy report by Srila Prabhupada. Krishna and the Supreme Personality of Godhead are identical, therefore Lord Krishna is referred to as Bhagawan throughout the Gita. Bhagawan is the ultimate in the Absolute Truth. Absolute Truth is realized in three phases of understanding, namely Brahman or the impersonal all-pervasive spirit, Paramatma or the centralized aspect of the Supreme within the heart of all living entities, and Bhagawan or the Supreme Personality of Godhead. In the Srimad Bhagavatam this conception of the Absolute Truth is explained thus: vadanti tattva vidas tattvam yajnana madhvayam brahmeti paramatmeti bhagavaneti shabdhyate. The Absolute Truth is realized in three phases of understanding by the knower of the Absolute Truth and all of them are identical. Such phases of the Absolute Truth are expressed as Brahman, Paramatma, and Bhagawan. These three Divine aspects can be explained by the example of the sun, which also has three different aspects, namely the sunshine, the sun's surface, and the sun planet itself. One who studies the sunshine only is the preliminary student, one who understands the sun's surface is further advanced, and one who can enter into the sun planet is the highest. Ordinary students who are satisfied by simply understanding the sunshine, its universal pervasiveness, and the glaring effulgence of its impersonal nature may be compared to those who can realize only the Brahman feature of the Absolute Truth. The student who has advanced further can know the sun disc, which is compared to knowledge of the Paramatma feature of the Absolute Truth, and the student who can enter into the heart of the Sun planet is compared to those who realize the personal features of the Supreme Absolute Truth. Therefore the bhaktas or the transcendentalists who have realized the Bhagawan feature of the Absolute Truth are the top most transcendentalists. Although all students who are engaged in the study of the Absolute Truth are engaged in the same subject matter, the sunshine, the sun disc, and the inner affairs of the Sun planet cannot be separated from one another, and yet the students of the three different phases are not in the same category. The Sanskrit word Bhagawan is explained by the great authority Parashara Muni, the father of Vyasa Deva: the Supreme personality who possesses all riches, all strength, all fame, all beauty, all knowledge, and all renunciation is called Bhagawan.

---
### Krishna's Supremacy, Aryan Values, Liberation
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/e3SxWTcHSKk?t=240
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Only Krishna can claim this because he is the Supreme personality of Godhead."
**Summary:** This segment continues to establish Krishna's supremacy, contrasting Him with other powerful beings, and then discusses Aryan values, emphasizing spiritual realization and liberation from material bondage.

There are many personalities possessing the qualities of Bhagawan, but Krishna is the Supreme because none can excel him. He's a Supreme person and his body is eternal, full of knowledge and Bliss. He is the Primeval Lord Govinda and the cause of all causes. In the bhagavatham also there is a list of many incarnations of the Supreme personality of Godhead, but Krishna is described as the original personality of Godhead from whom many many incarnations and personalities of Godhead expand. Krishna is the one who is eternal and full of knowledge and bliss, he is the Supreme personality whom many incarnations and personalities of Godhead expand. All the lists of the incarnations of Godhead submitted herewith are either plenary expansions or parts of the plenary expansions of the Supreme Godhead, but Krishna is the Supreme Personality of Godhead Himself. Therefore, Krishna is the original Supreme Personality of Godhead, the Absolute Truth, the source of both the Supersoul and the Impersonal Brahman. In the presence of the Supreme Personality of Godhead, Arjuna's lamentation for his kinsmen is certainly unbecoming, and therefore Krishna expressed His surprise with the word, kutas, wherefrom? Such unmanly sentiments were never expected from a person belonging to the civilized class of men known as Aryans. The word Aryan is applicable to persons who know the value of life and have a civilization based on spiritual realization. Persons who are led by the material conception of life do not know that the aim of life is really to achieve the goal of life. They are led by the realization of the Absolute Truth, Vishnu or Bhagavan, and they are captivated by the external features of the material world, and therefore they do not know what liberation is. Persons who have no knowledge of liberation from material bondage are called non-Aryans. Although Arjuna was a Kshatriya, he was deviating from his prescribed duties by declining to fight. This act of cowardice is described as befitting the non-Aryans. Such deviation from duty does not help one in the program, nor does it even give one the opportunity to become famous in this world. Lord Krishna did not approve of the so-called compassion of Arjuna for his kinsmen.

### Pure Devotee, Perfect Knowledge, Bhagavan's Qualities

To any human, even big big personality, they commit mistake. But Nārāyaṇa para, he is transcendental. Kṛṣṇa is transcendental. There cannot be any mistake. There cannot be any illusion. If your knowledge is imperfect, then whatever you speak, that is imperfect. Therefore with imperfect knowledge, why you should become a teacher? That is cheating. Therefore purposefully Vyāsadeva is writing śrī-bhagavān vāca, where there is no cheating, no imperfection, no illusion, no mistake, four things: no mistake, no illusion, no cheating, and no imperfection. This is bhagavān.

There are so many other books we can read, so many theories, so many philosophers, big big philosophers, but we cannot take them because they are defective. The author is sure to commit mistake, he is illusioned, because his senses are not perfect, therefore imperfection. So with all these defects we cannot accept anyone's knowledge. And if I receive the knowledge from bhagavān, and if I distribute the same knowledge as bhagavān has said, without any interpretation of my cheating policy, then the knowledge which I distribute, that is also perfect. ### Spiritual Master, Caitanya Mahaprabhu, Superior Authority
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/e3SxWTcHSKk?t=921

**Content Type:** analogy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers, Newcomers

**Summary:** Using the analogy of a peon delivering a money order, this segment explains how anyone can become a spiritual master by following the order of a superior authority, as emphasized by Caitanya Mahaprabhu.

I have given several times, just like a peon has brought a money order for you, thousand dollars. I have given a thousand dollars for you. Just like a peon has brought a money order for you, thousand dollars. Just like a peon has brought a money order for you, thousand dollars. So he is giving you. So you cannot say, here is a peon, he is a poor man, how he can give me one thousand dollars? He is not giving. The money is sent by somebody else. He is simply handing it over. Therefore Caitanya Mahāprabhu says āmā rāgdhāya guruhaiyā tāraḥ sarva-deśaḥ, he is asking everyone to become a spiritual master. So how everyone can become spiritual master? A spiritual master have sufficient knowledge and so many other qualification? No, even without any qualification one can become spiritual master. How? The process is Caitanya Mahāprabhu says āmā rāgdhāya guruhaiyā tāraḥ sarva-deśaḥ. Even without any qualification one can become spiritual master. How? On my order. That is the crucial point. One does not become spiritual master by his own wings. That is not spiritual master. He must be ordered by superior authority, then he is spiritual. Āmā rāgdhāya. Just like in our case, our superior authority, our spiritual master, he ordered me that you just try to preach this gospel, whatever you have learned from me in English. That I have tried to execute the order of superior authority. That's all. The only qualification is that I have tried to execute the order of superior authority. This is the secret of success.

Suppose here is big fire, just like we got fire place, that is in one corner, where the whole room you are feeling heat. That heat is impersonal. But the fire place where there is blazing fire, that is personal. So impersonal conception is the offshoot of the person. That will be explained in the 13th chapter. That everyone, everywhere I am spread. I exist everywhere. How does he exist? By his energy. That energy is impersonal. But the Supreme Person, he is not impersonal. He is personal.

### Guru qualification, order of Guru, rubber-stamped guru
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/S9Nfm8KMcZc?t=350
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "The key principle here is that to become guru, one must be ordered by one's guru."
**Summary:** The speaker continues to emphasize the importance of being ordered by one's Guru to become a Guru, contrasting this with the concept of a 'rubber-stamped' or unauthorized Guru.

And in small temple you have guru. That's all. No obligation, no preaching, simply brings a foodstuff, my Guru Mahārāj, joint mess, place for eating, our ātya khana, joint mess. Exactly. So we see here, Śrīla Prabhupāda emphasized that a rubber-stamped guru won't be effective. The key principle here is that to become guru, one must be ordered by one's guru. In other words, any person ordered by his guru to become guru is authorized. And any person who is not ordered by his guru, but he becomes guru, some or the other, either by himself or somebody else tells him, or there is a body of some people who give him a no objection to become a guru, some or the other, he becomes guru, then he is not bona fide, he is rubber-stamped or unauthorized guru.

### GBC meeting, questions, future of ISKCON
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/S9Nfm8KMcZc?t=673
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "After due deliberations in the meeting, the GBC chose five questions that they wanted answers from Srila Prabhupada for the time after his departure."
**Summary:** The speaker describes the GBC meeting in Vrindavan, noting that only 18 out of 23 members were present, and outlines the five questions they prepared to ask Srila Prabhupada regarding the future of ISKCON after his departure.

And they held a meeting in Vrindavan. At that time in ISKCON, there were 23 GBC members. But only 18 were able to make it to Vrindavan for the meeting. After due deliberations in the meeting, the GBC chose five questions that they wanted answers from Srila Prabhupada for the time after his departure. So the 18 GBC members were present there, noted down the five questions they wanted to ask Srila Prabhupada. What were those questions? The questions were, number one, how long should GBC members remain in office? Number two, how can GBC members who leave be replaced? So actually, you see, these two questions are relevant only in Prabhupada's disappearance. Because as long as Prabhupada was there, the GBC members were continuing and whoever was leaving, Prabhupada was replacing them. So this question was coming up because in future, when Prabhupada is not there, how will they do it? Question number three, in the absence of Srila Prabhupada, what is the procedure for first, second and sannyas initiations? Question number four, what is the relationship of the person who gives this initiation to the person he gives it to? And question number five, the last question, is there any provision for publication of other translations of Vaishnava scriptures by the BBT after the departure of Srila Prabhupada?

### Rithviks, July 9th directive, Srila Prabhupada's appointment
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/S9Nfm8KMcZc?t=1237
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Prabhupada immediately responded with officiating Acharyas. A clear, straight question and a clear, straight answer."
**Summary:** The speaker emphasizes that Srila Prabhupada's response to question three was to appoint officiating Acharyas or Rithviks, not Diksha Gurus, and that this was confirmed by the July 9th directive, which is not a temporary arrangement but meant for the time when Srila Prabhupada is appointed.

If Shaila Prabhupada wanted them to become Gurus, he could have said that he is going to recommend some of them to act as Diksha Gurus or Gurus. But no. The moment the question was put to Shaila Prabhupada, how initiations will be conducted in the future, particularly at that time, when Prabhupada is no longer with us, Shaila Prabhupada, without hesitating for a moment, or waiting to think, or considering different options, should we do like this, or should we have this system, or we have that system, there was no such consideration. Prabhupada immediately responded with officiating Acharyas. A clear, straight question and a clear, straight answer. And we all know that Shaila Prabhupada did choose eleven people to act as Rithvik, representative of the Acharya, which, in other words, is officiating Acharya. And when did Shaila Prabhupada do this? He did this in the July 9th, 1977 directive. Hence, the July 9th directive appointing Rithviks is not a temporary arrangement, but it is meant for the time, particularly when Shaila Prabhupada is appointed. It is not a temporary arrangement. But it is meant for the time, particularly when Shaila Prabhupada is appointed. It is meant for the time, particularly when Shaila Prabhupada is appointed.

### Guru, initiation, Rithvik, Srila Prabhupada
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/S9Nfm8KMcZc?t=1424
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "The person who is giving initiation, the initiator is the Guru. And the officiator is the Rithvik."
**Summary:** The speaker analyzes Srila Prabhupada's response to Satsvarupa Dasa's question, highlighting that Prabhupada reiterates the principle that without one's Guru's order, no one can become Guru, and clarifies that the person giving initiation (Srila Prabhupada) is the Guru, while the officiator is the Rithvik.

So, now, let us see what is Prabhupada's response to Satswaroop Dasa's question. Prabhupada, he is Guru. He is Guru, Satswaroop. But he does it on your behalf. Prabhupada, yes, that is formality. Because in my presence, one should not become Guru. So, on my behalf, on my order, Amar Ajnayi Guru Haya. Be actually Guru, but by my order. So, here, we can clearly see that Prabhupada is reiterating the same principle which he discussed in the April 22nd meeting, April 22nd discussion between Prabhupada and Tamalkrishna Goswami. Without one's Guru's order, no one can become Guru. Shaila Prabhupada was stating this principle. Another point to note here is that Satswaroop Dasa wanted to ask what is the relationship between the Rithvik and the devotee who is getting initiated. But instead, he ended up asking, what is the relationship between the person who gives initiation and the disciple? Actually, in Shaila Prabhupada's mind, it is clear that there are two people. One who gives initiation, which is Shaila Prabhupada, and the other one who officiates, which is the Rithvik. So, when Satswaroop Dasa asked what is the relationship of the person who gives initiation, and the disciple, Shaila Prabhupada immediately said that he is Guru. What does that mean? The person who is giving initiation, the initiator is the Guru. And the officiator is the Rithvik. Initiator is Shaila Prabhupada and he is Guru. It is very clear, abundantly clear.
